  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_9e9e7291-6863-4d12-9060-92b9b62aed2e'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>

        if (this.up('#box')) {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});

            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/108756-shelley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/108756-shelley?shelf=youth">youth</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer5253120" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12558115780924407781">This is the cutest book in the entire world. You kind of just want to hug it and squeeze it and call it George, because it's just that damned cute. <br/><br/>The subtitle is "part comedy, part love story, part everything-but-the-kitchen sink," and that's pretty accurate. I got a bit of a Princess Bride type of vibe from it. I just kept giggling throughout - totally mixed up fairy tale, just slightly surreal and a bit mocking. So much fun!<br/><br/>(Okay, there were some parts where the author was clearly trying too</span>
  <span id="freeText12558115780924407781" style="display:none">This is the cutest book in the entire world. You kind of just want to hug it and squeeze it and call it George, because it's just that damned cute. <br /><br />The subtitle is "part comedy, part love story, part everything-but-the-kitchen sink," and that's pretty accurate. I got a bit of a Princess Bride type of vibe from it. I just kept giggling throughout - totally mixed up fairy tale, just slightly surreal and a bit mocking. So much fun!<br /><br />(Okay, there were some parts where the author was clearly trying too hard to keep the tone and did a bit too much telling instead of showing- this was mostly evident with the three older sisters who came for the wedding. But by that time, I was so involved that it only registered as a minor annoyance, and the end was back to the original level of fun. I kind of wonder if an editor was responsible for those pages, because they stick out.)</span>

<div id="review_72689129" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/72689129" />

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer72689129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17453736265758769066">OH. MY. CUTENESS.<br/><br/>This book was awesome! And, okay, I DO happen to have a thing for cheesy young-adult romance fairy-tales, but still, it was really clever and totally adorable! And CLEAN. I wouldn't hesitate to read this book to an 8-year-old (or younger, if they were interested). It was predictable (I guessed who Christian was in the first chapter, but whatever... the goal of the book wasn't to be cryptic), but it was just so sweet and innocent and SO funny!<br/><br/>Okay, so it's about this 6-year-old b</span>
  <span id="freeText17453736265758769066" style="display:none">OH. MY. CUTENESS.<br /><br />This book was awesome! And, okay, I DO happen to have a thing for cheesy young-adult romance fairy-tales, but still, it was really clever and totally adorable! And CLEAN. I wouldn't hesitate to read this book to an 8-year-old (or younger, if they were interested). It was predictable (I guessed who Christian was in the first chapter, but whatever... the goal of the book wasn't to be cryptic), but it was just so sweet and innocent and SO funny!<br /><br />Okay, so it's about this 6-year-old boy, Christian, who runs away from home and ends up living with and being raised by a Troll, Edric (Ed) in a cave. The kid turns out to be quite nice and resourceful (i.e. he's an inventor). Ed realizes he's gotta raise the kid right, so he gets a book of etiquette, and teaches the kid out of that. But the best part is that Ed has like ZERO grasp of clichÃ©s, and is CONSTANTLY mixing them up (like, "I can see I'm beating my head against a dead horse" and "After all, what's sauce for the goose is sauce for the eager beaver.") Oh boy, those were great... <br /><br />So 13 years later, Christian (sometimes Chris) is a strapping guy... haha... And he has this telescope, and has been (very innocently) admiring the pretty little brunette princess (Marigold, 17) whose balcony happens to face the cave... ;) In fact, he's so taken with her that he starts sending her messages via carrier pigeon. Heehee... But the pigeons can only hold a piece of paper big enough to hold 3 lines of text (and later 3 per side, I think), so they have these TINY conversations... It's REALLY cute. They become best friends, even though they've never met. <br /><br />Then Christian and Ed decide he needs to go out on his own and experience the world, so he gets a job at the castle, and all sorts of craziness ensues... Marigold's mom is trying to hook her up with any eligible bachelor who will have her, and Christian is REALLY jealous... *cute!!* And it's really fun... <br /><br />Anyway, it goes on from there, but I don't want to give TOO much away. I'm REALLY looking forward to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2430999.Twice_Upon_a_Marigold__Upon_a_Marigold___2_" title="Twice Upon a Marigold (Upon a Marigold, #2) by Jean Ferris" rel="nofollow noopener">Twice Upon a Marigold</a>... It looks really great, too!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17453736265758769066" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6056859144492206065">I totally judged a book by its cover on this one. The font the words are printed in reminded me of the font from Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants (easy read, I knew), and it proclaimed itself to be â€œpart comedy, part love story, part everything-but-the-kitchen-sink; happily-ever-after turned upside down, inside out, and completely over the top!â€ Well, I donâ€™t know about all that, but it was an entertaining read â€” a fairy tale with a modern, fun, whimsical feel to it.<br/><br/>I must admit I liked the fir</span>
  <span id="freeText6056859144492206065" style="display:none">I totally judged a book by its cover on this one. The font the words are printed in reminded me of the font from Sisterhood of the Traveling Pants (easy read, I knew), and it proclaimed itself to be â€œpart comedy, part love story, part everything-but-the-kitchen-sink; happily-ever-after turned upside down, inside out, and completely over the top!â€ Well, I donâ€™t know about all that, but it was an entertaining read â€” a fairy tale with a modern, fun, whimsical feel to it.<br /><br />I must admit I liked the first half of the story much better than the second half. It seems that the first half is spent getting attached to the main characters in the story: Christian (a runaway who is raised by a troll) and Ed (the aforementioned troll who can never get his cliches right and is obsessed with dethroning the Tooth Fairy) and Marigold (a cursed princess who becomes Christianâ€™s penpal). I came to like them. I loved their "p-mailing" (pigeon-carrier mailing) back and forth. But then we donâ€™t get to spend any time with them in the second half of the book. Peripheral characters (mostly Marigoldâ€™s dad and her triplet sisters) get turned into main characters, too, so their stories have to be told â€” and all the while Chris and Ed are in the dungeon, out of sight and out of mind. My only guess as to why the kingâ€™s and the sistersâ€™ stories took the limelight was because they hadnâ€™t proven to be particularly sympathetic to Marigold in the past, and they needed to explain themselves so it would make sense when they band together to save her from the queenâ€™s evil scheme.<br /><br />But other than that complaint, I liked this book. There was just the right amount of quirkiness and just the right amount of seriousness. A quick, fun read.<br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4994265432886115668">I unabashedly love children's books, but this was even too juvenile for me. <br/><br/>Marigold is a strong-willed princess who is being forced to marry a prince she doesn't love. Christian is a bright young man who doesn't realize he's actually a prince. You already know how this is going to end. Beyond being predictable, the story tries very hard to have an irreverent, almost Shrek-like tone. But it fails by being unfunny and weighed down by trite concepts like p-mail (it's like email but with pigeons, g</span>
  <span id="freeText4994265432886115668" style="display:none">I unabashedly love children's books, but this was even too juvenile for me. <br /><br />Marigold is a strong-willed princess who is being forced to marry a prince she doesn't love. Christian is a bright young man who doesn't realize he's actually a prince. You already know how this is going to end. Beyond being predictable, the story tries very hard to have an irreverent, almost Shrek-like tone. But it fails by being unfunny and weighed down by trite concepts like p-mail (it's like email but with pigeons, get it?!?!)<br /><br />The dialogue, especially between Christian and Marigold, is painful. They are each others dear hearts and soul mates and every other sappy term you can think of. While there are some sweet parts and some interesting characters, it's all just too corny and goofy. There are so many good children's books out there, especially in the fantasy genre, that this just falls completely flat in comparison. </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/163813644" />
    <a title="Amy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/844731-amy"><img alt="Amy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1305861377p2/844731.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/844731-amy">Amy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/844731-amy?shelf=children">children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/844731-amy?shelf=2011">2011</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer163813644" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7274048119675637724">5/10<br/>I feel bad giving this such a low rating because I think there are a lot of young girls who would really, really like it. But, for me, it was just too juvenile...and that's coming from someone who LOVES children's and young adult literature.<br/><br/>I know it's a little unfair to say that a middle-grade book (written for 9-12 year-olds) was "too juvenile." But I'm comparing it to other books for the same age group (The Miraculous Journey of Edward Tulane, anyone?), and it can't even hold a candle aga</span>
  <span id="freeText7274048119675637724" style="display:none">5/10<br />I feel bad giving this such a low rating because I think there are a lot of young girls who would really, really like it. But, for me, it was just too juvenile...and that's coming from someone who LOVES children's and young adult literature.<br /><br />I know it's a little unfair to say that a middle-grade book (written for 9-12 year-olds) was "too juvenile." But I'm comparing it to other books for the same age group (The Miraculous Journey of Edward Tulane, anyone?), and it can't even hold a candle against some of them.<br /><br />First of all, the characters all say dumb things that I guess are supposed to be funny. For example, from Marigold: "I'd rather be boiled in oil! The kind with cholesterol!" See? Painful. Then there's the troll who is constantly taking well-known phrases and accidentally changing them just enough that they make no sense at all. This is also supposed to be funny. The problem is, a 9-12 year-old is not going to know what the real phrase is so she won't be able to catch the humor, and it isn't clever enough for an adult to think it's funny. So, fail and fail.<br /><br />The plot itself was boring and predictable. Christian wants to meet Marigold. Done. Christian wants Marigold to like him. Done. Christian wants to be more than a peasant. Done. There were, um, count them, ZERO moments of tension. (Okay, I'm probably being a little harsh since a 9-year-old probably would have felt some drama in the dungeon or during the wedding...yes, there was a dungeon...for about 8 hours...really nail-biting). <br /><br />So here's my final take: I've been reading so many long books lately that I was just looking for something short and easy. This definitely fit the bill, but it made me ready to go back to more thought-provoking books. Also, a nine-year-old girl will like this book. I promise.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7274048119675637724" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText8736629452124901787" style="display:none">What do you get when you mix an evil mother, a not so typical princess, a grumpy troll and a lost boy? Things take a turn for the worse though when Christian discovers that Marigoldâ€™s mother Queen Olympia is planning to take over the kingdom and even willing to sacrifice her own daughter to do so. Christian must do everything in his power to protect his love and find his own destiny in the process. <br />Themes:<br />World of make believe (story takes place in another world with magical creatures)<br />Loyalty to others (Christianâ€™s loyalty to Marigold)<br />Love in different forms (Not only love for a significant other but also love for a parent, sibling or animal)<br />Masked intentions of different characters (There are a lot of intentions that are hidden from the reader as the book goes along)<br /></span>

  <span id="freeText2180236662882312398" style="display:none">This book is just as cute as a pile of puppies and kittens licking each other's ears on a glittery pink blanket. Surrounded by cupcakes.<br /><br />That is to say, there's a certain audience for this kind of thing and everyone else should keep their cute-sickness bags handy. (I am saying this as a fan of Cute Overload with a very high tolerance for cuteness.) <br /><br />It's the light and fluffy side of a fairy tale without the darkness.<br /><br />But it isn't bad. Ed and Christian are relatively enlightened buddies. While Princess Marigold is smart (though not very funny), confident, and gutsy. The bad guys are appropriately evil, boorish, and dull with few redeeming qualities. <br /><br />The plot rolls along pleasantly enough. And it kept me entertained while I read it.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8960977206197757878">"Once Upon a Marigold" is a romantic comedy book. In the story, a commoner who lives in a cave with a troll and two dogs falls in love with the youngest princess of their kingdom. They start off as best friends through "p-mail" (basically handwritten letters sent by pigeons), but soon they meet at one point in the book and become something more. This is a very cheesy book filled with corny jokes, so I think only a few section of readers would enjoy reading this and apparently I'm a part of that </span>
  <span id="freeText8960977206197757878" style="display:none">"Once Upon a Marigold" is a romantic comedy book. In the story, a commoner who lives in a cave with a troll and two dogs falls in love with the youngest princess of their kingdom. They start off as best friends through "p-mail" (basically handwritten letters sent by pigeons), but soon they meet at one point in the book and become something more. This is a very cheesy book filled with corny jokes, so I think only a few section of readers would enjoy reading this and apparently I'm a part of that "few section".</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4630593640222540523">4.5<br/><b>Reader thoughts:</b> I almost put the book down on page two. So glad I didn't! (It starts with an old man walking through the woods. Not interesting, until you find out he's a troll.)<br/><br/>The book's climax reminded me of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24337.Ella_Enchanted' title='Ella Enchanted by Gail Carson Levine' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ella Enchanted</a>. There was a curse to break, a step-mother to face, a prince to marry, people shouting, and a dog-powered flying machine (okay, not exactly like <i>Ella Enchanted</i>). Fun though, and lots happening at once.<br/><br/>The relationship between Christian and his foster father was well-don</span>
  <span id="freeText4630593640222540523" style="display:none">4.5<br /><b>Reader thoughts:</b> I almost put the book down on page two. So glad I didn't! (It starts with an old man walking through the woods. Not interesting, until you find out he's a troll.)<br /><br />The book's climax reminded me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24337.Ella_Enchanted" title="Ella Enchanted by Gail Carson Levine" rel="nofollow noopener">Ella Enchanted</a>. There was a curse to break, a step-mother to face, a prince to marry, people shouting, and a dog-powered flying machine (okay, not exactly like <i>Ella Enchanted</i>). Fun though, and lots happening at once.<br /><br />The relationship between Christian and his foster father was well-done. It wasn't saccharine, it wasn't bitter, but it was practical. Both accepted the other for what they were, inventor or collector, tooth-business entrepreneur or secret-messages-sending stalker.<br /><br />The villain was well-done. I kept thinking, "This is too easy," but then the good guys would get locked up again. The villain wasn't stupid; she knew what was going on and took reasonable measures to stop it.<br /><br /><b>Writer thoughts:</b> The pov was omniscient, and I wonder why. Maybe it was to sound a little like fairytales. Maybe it was to give a more complete approach to the story (like seeing into the doctor's head at the climax; perfect! That made me laugh out loud for over a minute). There were quite a few times I wished the pov was more limited, though.<br /><br />Why a sequel? As much as I liked this book, I wouldn't want a sequel. It would be like trying to write a sequel to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24337.Ella_Enchanted" title="Ella Enchanted by Gail Carson Levine" rel="nofollow noopener">Ella Enchanted</a>, which is perfect by itself. I'd have to read it to decide, but I feel like it wouldn't fit at all. The people are married, and everything's tied up! Olympia has no power that a conniving author doesn't give her.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4630593640222540523" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16856938746137261045">I picked up this book because a friend of mine really enjoyed it. I tried to get into it, because there were a couple of cute ideas in the book, but in the end the writing was simply too poor to keep me engaged.   <span id="freeText16856938746137261045" style="display:none">I picked up this book because a friend of mine really enjoyed it. I tried to get into it, because there were a couple of cute ideas in the book, but in the end the writing was simply too poor to keep me engaged. Every time I managed to get involved in the story for a few paragraphs, I would be tossed out of the story again by a particularly awkward bit of exposition. The characters weren't well-developed (with the possible exception of Marigold), and the plot was slow-moving and awkwardly contrived, IMO. <br /><br />It wasn't the cuteness or silliness of the book that I minded. A cute, silly book was exactly what I wanted to read this weekend. If only the writing hadn't been so poor....</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16568568880392037727">I need to not read any Medievalish fantasy ever again, especially the truncated and sterilized version in novels for kids. All I can do is think "marriage alliances do not work that way" and "living in a castle was way dirtier than that" and "the politics of a monarchy are just ... NOT THAT WAY." I also really disliked the narrative style of this audiobook and found the plot just sickeningly predictable. I knew I'd hate it once I came across the phrase "p-mail" - shudder. Of course I see the app</span>
  <span id="freeText16568568880392037727" style="display:none">I need to not read any Medievalish fantasy ever again, especially the truncated and sterilized version in novels for kids. All I can do is think "marriage alliances do not work that way" and "living in a castle was way dirtier than that" and "the politics of a monarchy are just ... NOT THAT WAY." I also really disliked the narrative style of this audiobook and found the plot just sickeningly predictable. I knew I'd hate it once I came across the phrase "p-mail" - shudder. Of course I see the appeal to the right audience, but the right audience is definitely not me.</span>

<div id="review_2095924181" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2095924181" />
    <a title="Moriah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5599840-moriah"><img alt="Moriah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573006971p2/5599840.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2095924181?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Moriah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Moriah" href="/user/show/5599840-moriah">Moriah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2095924181" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14065733467107590229">I'm a sucker for a good romance. Really, I'm weak when it comes to romantic gestures. <br/><br/>The book began with Christian, a six-year-old, that ran away from home being found in the forest by a troll, Ed. The humor of the story, the ridiculousness of it, began here. From the beginning the dialogue contained a light, airy, and modern quality that didn't fit with the time period common with princes and princess. The anachronistic air reminded me of <i>The Princess Bride</i>. Since it's one of my favorite roman</span>
  <span id="freeText14065733467107590229" style="display:none">I'm a sucker for a good romance. Really, I'm weak when it comes to romantic gestures. <br /><br />The book began with Christian, a six-year-old, that ran away from home being found in the forest by a troll, Ed. The humor of the story, the ridiculousness of it, began here. From the beginning the dialogue contained a light, airy, and modern quality that didn't fit with the time period common with princes and princess. The anachronistic air reminded me of <i>The Princess Bride</i>. Since it's one of my favorite romantic comedies, even though it wasn't my favorite book, it convinced me to continue reading. <br /><br />While this is categorized as a young adult, it felt more like a middle grade novel to me. For someone looking for something light and quick to read, this is the way to go. I read most of it in one sitting and would finish entire chapters without even realizing that I was reading. <br /><br />One of my friends sent me this book and said that I would fall for Christian, and I did! He took things with Marigold slowly, first by p-mail (contact through pigeons) and then when he met her in person, he didn't force himself on her. He was romantic without even trying to be, and she wasn't wrong about me falling for him. <br /><br />I haven't decided if I'm going to continue the series yet, considering the book does have some sense of finality, but I am curious to know what could happen next. <i>Once Upon A Marigold</i> appeals to fans of <i>Ella Enchanted</i> and <i>The Princess Bride</i>. It was funny and light and there were moments when it was difficult not to break out in a ridiculous smile.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14065733467107590229" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer727232940168067764">I'm writing this at like 10pm and my ADHD meds have long worn off, so forgive the scattered tone of this review.<br/>I'm working my way out of a horrendous reading slump right now (that has lasted for over a year), and I'm pleased to say time flew as these pages did.   <span id="freeText727232940168067764" style="display:none">I'm writing this at like 10pm and my ADHD meds have long worn off, so forgive the scattered tone of this review.<br />I'm working my way out of a horrendous reading slump right now (that has lasted for over a year), and I'm pleased to say time flew as these pages did. For the first time in a long time, I lost myself in my reading, somehow not annoying my roommate with my overexcited exclamations and comments from time to time (but only because I have such a great roommate and not because I wasn't making overexcited exclamations and comments because believe me, I was!)<br />This book brought me back to the summer my sister took me to the library and I checked out 15 books, and my sister said to only take like half of them because there was no way I could finish 15 books in three weeks (or maybe it was 12 books, idk, it was a very long time ago, I was like 13, give me a break), and I took that as a personal challenge (since I was already grounded from electronics for the summer, so like, what else was I gonna do with my time?). I finished them all. And then went back to the library for more books. It was a good summer. Reading this book today felt like that. I've really been missing the ability to lose myself in a good book like that.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780613716376" href="/book/show/2976930-once-upon-a-marigold">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68146783-madao?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68146783-madao?shelf=romance-meh">romance-meh</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2361113836" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3201971636678621868">So after The Girl with the Dragon Tattoo which almost killed my brain (in a good way, of course) I decided to pick up this book, because I love fairy-tale like stories. This book did a good job at making me feel alive again. <br/>As usual, we have a commoner handsome but nice boy, an ill king, a princess and a scheming, evil queen in this book too. There were lots of cliches, but this book was so innocent and cute, I couldn't complain at all. The romance made me warm, and the foster family of Christi</span>
  <span id="freeText3201971636678621868" style="display:none">So after The Girl with the Dragon Tattoo which almost killed my brain (in a good way, of course) I decided to pick up this book, because I love fairy-tale like stories. This book did a good job at making me feel alive again. <br />As usual, we have a commoner handsome but nice boy, an ill king, a princess and a scheming, evil queen in this book too. There were lots of cliches, but this book was so innocent and cute, I couldn't complain at all. The romance made me warm, and the foster family of Christian which included the troll and his dogs were equally good. There were no complicated schemes, the writing was easy to understand, and overall I felt really good when I read this book. Because who doesn't like happy endings? Though I kind of didn't really appreciate the part where <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ we get to know Christian is a prince after all, because honestly, when there will come a time when commoners get beautiful princesses? Nevermind that, though.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />I was lazy to complete it at times, but this book was perfect. It surely joined among the list of books I would love to read to my nieces or nephews (if I have any) in future.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3123571530?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Powers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Powers" href="/user/show/90929860-sarah-powers">Sarah Powers</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3123571530" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8985850037075335368">3.5 stars. Tbh, this was a reread. I read this as a young teen and of course loved it then. Therefore, I was excited to see it on my sister's shelf and refresh my memory with a rereading. Funny and zanny humor (Ed and his mixed metaphors are life!). It is sweet and refreshing. Of course, reading with a more mature and developed literary palette it was not faultless. It definitely falls in to a strong "tell vs. show" narrative, especially as the story progresses, which at this point in my reading</span>
  <span id="freeText8985850037075335368" style="display:none">3.5 stars. Tbh, this was a reread. I read this as a young teen and of course loved it then. Therefore, I was excited to see it on my sister's shelf and refresh my memory with a rereading. Funny and zanny humor (Ed and his mixed metaphors are life!). It is sweet and refreshing. Of course, reading with a more mature and developed literary palette it was not faultless. It definitely falls in to a strong "tell vs. show" narrative, especially as the story progresses, which at this point in my reading life I generally find very annoying. However, keeping in mind the target audience (preteens), I can't fault that too much, as I remember wanting all of my own suspicions confirmed and spelled out so that I knew I was right in my hypothesis of the characters and plot. A little cliche in parts, but overall incredibly funny and fresh.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8985850037075335368" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('L6o1iHIjndbCTjDb3dduK/0bxS6ESjcRRuYtqlcdHbJXUcZInh6HKKQJAEjiApyYAH4vUinKMojA9OpFBIMxEQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tztPge2+yT8o1JAJKCLmQOWgup6oztipIlD3GXZ3oAjPwLxBAYPTwU6ToJoX9xTzGMVQ4gVO3TCkQjD2JemMqw==')})

<span id="freeTextContainer5135785324968405510">This author is not afraid to tackle difficult subjects: living with a deaf parent (Of Sound Mind), facing the consequences of a criminal act (Bad), or questioning one's sexuality (Eight Seconds). But Jean Ferris is also adept at writing comedy, historical fiction, and romance. What's most interesting is that she didn't publish her first novel until she was in her mid-40s. Yet she's never forgotten</span>
  <span id="freeText5135785324968405510" style="display:none">This author is not afraid to tackle difficult subjects: living with a deaf parent (Of Sound Mind), facing the consequences of a criminal act (Bad), or questioning one's sexuality (Eight Seconds). But Jean Ferris is also adept at writing comedy, historical fiction, and romance. What's most interesting is that she didn't publish her first novel until she was in her mid-40s. Yet she's never forgotten the intense feelings and changes of her own teenage years. Critics as well as teen readers have seen the evidence of that in her writing and have honored her novels with a number of awards, from Best Books for Young Adults to various state and National Book Award nominations.</span>
